    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

<span id="freeTextContainer5892259056885535559">As surprising as it is moving, The Storied Life of A. J. Fikry is an unforgettable tale of transformation and second chances, an irresistible affirmation of why we read, and why we love.<br/><br/>We are not quite novels.<br/><br/>We are not quite short stories.<br/><br/>In the end, we are collected works.<br/><br/>A.   <span id="freeText5892259056885535559" style="display:none">As surprising as it is moving, The Storied Life of A. J. Fikry is an unforgettable tale of transformation and second chances, an irresistible affirmation of why we read, and why we love.<br /><br />We are not quite novels.<br /><br />We are not quite short stories.<br /><br />In the end, we are collected works.<br /><br />A. J. Fikry's life is not at all what he expected it to be. His wife has died; his bookstore is experiencing the worst sales in its history; and now his prized possession, a rare collection of Poe poems, has been stolen. Slowly but surely, he is isolating himself from all the people of Alice Island—from Chief Lambiase, the well-intentioned police officer who's always felt kindly toward him; from Ismay, his sister-in-law, who is hell-bent on saving A.J. from his dreary self; from Amelia, the lovely and idealistic (if eccentric) Knightley Press sales rep who persists in taking the ferry to Alice Island, refusing to be deterred by A.J.'s bad attitude. Even the books in his store have stopped holding pleasure for him. These days, he can only see them as a sign of a world that is changing too rapidly.<br /><br />And then a mysterious package appears at the bookstore. It's a small package, though large in weight—an unexpected arrival that gives A.J. the opportunity to make his life over, the ability to see everything anew. It doesn't take long for the locals to notice the change overcoming A.J., for the determined sales rep Amelia to see her curmudgeonly client in a new light, for the wisdom of all those books to become again the lifeblood of A.J.'s world. Or for everything to twist again into a version of his life that he didn't see coming.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5892259056885535559" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div id="review_764083982" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/764083982" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5875398-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599578317p2/5875398.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/764083982?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/5875398-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5875398-rebecca?shelf=read-via-edelweiss">read-via-edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5875398-rebecca?shelf=bibliophiles-delight">bibliophiles-delight</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer764083982" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4942534642457567260">I’m starting to think I’m the only bibliophile on earth who didn’t care for this book. After everything I’d read about it, I didn’t think it could possibly fail to be fantastic. For me, though, it tips way too far into chick lit and YA territory, and succumbs too often (and too early) to schmaltz and melodrama.<br/><br/>Now, there are certainly some good points. A.J. himself, an independent bookseller and just-coping widower, is a delightfully irascible character with some decided literary prejudices that</span>
  <span id="freeText4942534642457567260" style="display:none">I’m starting to think I’m the only bibliophile on earth who didn’t care for this book. After everything I’d read about it, I didn’t think it could possibly fail to be fantastic. For me, though, it tips way too far into chick lit and YA territory, and succumbs too often (and too early) to schmaltz and melodrama.<br /><br />Now, there are certainly some good points. A.J. himself, an independent bookseller and just-coping widower, is a delightfully irascible character with some decided literary prejudices that I can certainly affirm: no series, no genre mash-ups, no celebrity memoirs, and – please, dear God – no vampires. Zevin’s literary references range from the classical to the contemporary and are bang on-trend (e.g. Alice Munro and David Foster Wallace).<br /><br />I truly enjoyed the first two chapters, with the quaint mystery of the stolen Poe first edition, and as a believer in bibliotherapy I appreciated Zevin’s insistence on “the necessity of encountering stories at precisely the right time in our lives.” I could even stomach the burgeoning romance between A.J. and Amelia, the quirky Knightley Press sales rep who takes the ferry out from Hyannis to visit Island Books. “Her specialty is persnickety little bookstores and the particular breed that runs them,” so it seems she’s found the perfect place. <br /><br />Then comes Chapter 3 and its plot twist, so coyly avoided by the jacket blurb but so central to the plot that I hardly think it’s worth calling it a spoiler: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[widower A.J. adopts Maya, a little girl abandoned in the store’s children’s section by her mother, a suicidal Harvard student. Come on, the baby on the doorstep – can you get any more clichéd than that?! Then, as Maya grows into a young woman, A.J. and Amelia try to make the relationship between a New York City working girl and a small-town entrepreneur work. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It seems A.J.’s “porcupine heart” is finally softening. Awwwwwwwwww. As the novel continues, it becomes more and more like a YA romance, especially with the increasing focus on <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Maya, who has unrealistically precocious speech and creative writing <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />The disastrous event A.J. holds with the author of Amelia’s favorite memoir is good fun, but in general I didn’t much enjoy the last two-thirds of the book. The romance plot is boring and predictable; the mystery elements are solved too neatly and unrealistically; a debate over whether e-readers will replace paper books is shoehorned in; and the foreshadowing is as subtle as a brick to the head. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So then A.J. gets sick. Cue maudlin conversations, cheer-inducing fundraising, and community-pulling-together slush. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I’m sorry, am I just a big cynic? The novel soon descends into a third-rate knock-off of <i>The Fault in Our Stars</i> (a book I loved, by the way, and one of the few YA gems I’ve found). <br /><br />Here’s my main problem with the book: it doesn’t know what it wants to be. Does it mean to be a quaint romance, an independent bookstore lover’s <i>Guernsey Literary and Potato Peel Pie Society</i>? If so, the gratuitous swearing and one-night stands will offend your more traditional types. Zevin should have made Fikry a restrained Anglo-Indian hermit in Hay-on-Wye instead. Or is it an edgy, youthful take on some chick lit tropes? If that’s the case, haters (like me) will object to the frequently sentimental content.<br /><br />The book helped me pass a flight to America pleasantly enough back in March, but as I go back through my notes and scan some newspaper reviews to write it up for <i>Bookmarks</i>, I’m reminded of everything I found so frustrating about it. “Everything is explained, and all the loose ends are tied up with a bow,” Keith Donohue wrote in his <a href="http://www.washingtonpost.com/entertainment/books/book-review-indie-bookstore-owner-inhabits-gabrielle-zevins-storied-life-of-aj-fikry/2014/03/31/a30f71c8-b6b8-11e3-8cc3-d4bf596577eb_story.html" rel="nofollow noopener"><i>Washington Post</i> review</a>. Well, if you ask me, that’s not always a good thing.<br /><br />A <b>
  <i>big</i>
</b> disappointment for this bibliophile, especially given the novel’s great potential.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4942534642457567260" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer911433774" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4776282011747786096">5+<br/><br/><i>We read to know we're not alone. We read because we are alone. We read and we are not alone. We are not alone.</i><br/><br/>Once in a while a book comes along that captures your heart and soul- where the characters become like friends and family, and a part of you wants to pack a bag and travel to that magical place forever. At the start you just know it is going to be something special- by the end you feel physical pain knowing that these people are gone from your life...One day you may pick it back up to </span>
  <span id="freeText4776282011747786096" style="display:none">5+<br><br><i>We read to know we're not alone. We read because we are alone. We read and we are not alone. We are not alone.</i><br><br>Once in a while a book comes along that captures your heart and soul- where the characters become like friends and family, and a part of you wants to pack a bag and travel to that magical place forever. At the start you just know it is going to be something special- by the end you feel physical pain knowing that these people are gone from your life...One day you may pick it back up to read again - but you know it will never be the same as that first experience. THE STORIED LIFE OF A.J. FIKRY made me smile, laugh out loud, cry uncontrollably...and my grinchy heart might have even grown three sizes. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400436654i/9676182.jpg" alt=" photo 5faa54bb-7f6d-4009-8044-6f8d854263ad_zpsc7ff9c77.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>39 year-old A.J. Fikry is the owner of a failing bookstore -Island Books- on Alice Island- it should be successful- being the only bookstore in the area and because of A.J.'s passion for books...but A.J. doesn't like people very much. His wife- Nic- was the people person, the one that kept the bookstore running, the love of his life- and now she is dead- killed in a car accident a year and a half ago...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400437681i/9676278.jpg" alt=" photo a4321eaa-5e4d-497b-9377-0fa6c4577f0a_zpsa0322070.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>...For the last year and a half A.J. has been barely getting by- he drinks too much, lives on frozen dinners, has stopped exercising, pushes people away, and is even grumpy to his staff and customers...but at least he has a plan- Sell the bookstore and auction off his copy of Tamerlane. An extremely rare collection of poems by Edgar Allan Poe- worth 400 thousand dollars. Then he can retire. But fate steps in and throws another gut-wrenching blow at Mr. Fikry- when the uninsured Tamerlane is stolen right out of his home during a night of binge drinking. It is the first wake up call A.J gets. The second is only weeks away...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400436654i/9676184.jpg" alt=" photo 7021bfc1-ce13-43d5-aaae-e05345798fe4_zps42cba728.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I will leave my review right there- because I think part of loving this book came from knowing practically nothing about it. It was full of so many little and BIG surprises along the way and I am soooooo glad I went against my first instinct of passing this one by. THE STORIED LIFE OF A.J. FIKRY is a story of love, loss, and second chances. I cannot recommend this one enough!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400437237i/9676239.jpg" alt=" photo 248b6007-4e5c-4f3b-9562-7f17f99ebd52_zps80fb30dd.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I won an advanced reader's copy from First-Reads.</span>

<div id="review_952767449" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/952767449" />
    <a title="Alejandro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro"><img alt="Alejandro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328672389p2/665584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/952767449?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Alejandro by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1283951-idarah">Idarah</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=book-about-books">book-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer952767449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10514112865341417466"><b>
  <i>Every word the right one and exactly where it should be. That's basically the highest compliment I can give...</i>
</b><br/><br/>...and I am truly glad that it didn't took me so long to read it!!!<br/><br/><b>
  <i>The words you can't find, you borrow...</i>
</b> <br/><br/>Maybe I could find the words but honestly, that first quote from this wonderful book was the right way to compliment it. And to do that, well I quote a second one too. <br/><br/>And you will find several quotes in this review since honestly, this is one of the most quotable novels tha</span>
  <span id="freeText10514112865341417466" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Every word the right one and exactly where it should be. That's basically the highest compliment I can give...</i>
</b><br /><br />...and I am truly glad that it didn't took me so long to read it!!!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>The words you can't find, you borrow...</i>
</b> <br /><br />Maybe I could find the words but honestly, that first quote from this wonderful book was the right way to compliment it. And to do that, well I quote a second one too. <br /><br />And you will find several quotes in this review since honestly, this is one of the most quotable novels that I ever read. And believe it or not, they won't be all the quotes that I loved here.<br /><br /><b>I LOVE THIS BOOK AND IT'S ONE OF THE BEST NOVELS THAT I EVER READ!</b><br /><br />And that it isn't a quote! That's my honest thinking about it!<br /><br />I have read several positive reviews about the novel and I was expecting a good book, but I never expected that it will be SOOOOOO good and a truly wonderful reading experience!<br /><br />This is a book about books. I mean, this story is about novels, novellas, short stories, readers, writers, bookstores... so indeed I think that this a "must-read" to every person with passion for reading and love for books.<br /><br />The style of the novel is quite particular since it's without a question a novel per se but each chapter is constructed as a kinda self-contained short story but all of them are one big storyline. And a priceless detail is that each chapter is titled for some famous short story written by some other author in the past and that it's related in some way to something on the chapter.<br /><br />A good book has characters with evolution and due that... this is an exceptional book! Since the evolution of each character is truly remarkable and taking unsuspected paths but all of them interconnected in such wonderful way. Even characters that you don't expect much at first, they will surprise you totally.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>A place isn't a place until it has a bookstore.</i>
</b><br /><br />I love Alice Island! I didn't want to reseach if Alice Island was a real place or not until finishing the book and the author explained that it was an invented place. Maybe it will sound odd, but I love that it is a fictional place. Since from the beginning I was playing the idea of that the place got its name from the <i>Alice</i> from <i>Wonderland</i>, that it's one of my favorite fairy tales, and while that wasn't confirmed on the novel, there was a reference to the tale, so there is hope...<br /><br /><b>
  <i>...the necessity of encountering stories at precisely the right time in our lives.</i>
</b><br /><br />Definitely, I want to believe that about this wonderful book, while it was published until this year (2014), so I wouldn't be able to read it before, still, it was the right time for me, since it would be very likely that even two years ago, I wouldn't be able to appreciate it in the same way.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>...the things we respond to at twenty are not necessarily the same things we will respond to at forty and vice versa. This is true in books and also in life.</i>
</b><br /><br />Definitely, we aren't the same people twice, each year we change for better or worse and that's why that you also never read the same book twice, maybe the first time you hate it and twenty years later you got amazed for the same novel. Experiences in life define how we perceive the following things on it.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>...forcing kids to read books like that that make them think they hate reading.</i>
</b><br /><br />Never force a book to a kid, even if you think that you are doing them a favor. That's why usually kids and even more teenagers hate to read the assigned books in schools. Let them find their genres, let them find their kind of books. Everybody is a reader, only some of them are still looking for the right book.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>...the easiest way to get old is to be technologically behind.</i>
</b><br /><br />Don't fight between paper books and e-readers. I love my printed books but now I am used to read several stuff on my tablet. For me, the important thing is to read, not matter in which way, but to read. Any book in any way. Just read.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Most people's problems would be solved if they would only give more things a chance.</i>
</b><br /><br />So, let's give it a chance to this novel! Maybe your problem won't be solved reading this book, but certainly it will put your soul at peace and with that, being able to find a solution.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>P.S.</i>
</b><br /><br />I am accountant but luckily the book that impacted me most in my life wasn't... <i>Principles of Accounting, Part II</i> !!! <br /><br />Not even close! Hahaha!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>P.P.S.</i>
</b><br /><br />Siberian huskies in Arizona?!! Only me found that odd? Hehehe!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>P.P.P.S.</i>
</b><br /><br />The old kind cops rule! 'Nuff said!!!<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10514112865341417466" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1129384405" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1129384405" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1129384405?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1129384405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15648484623870154382"><i>
  <b>"There ain't nobody in the world like book people."</b>
</i><br/><br/>It's a bit embarrassing to admit how emotional this book made me. I'm not even a fan of Zevin's work; I quite liked the concept behind <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/359410.Elsewhere' title='Elsewhere by Gabrielle Zevin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Elsewhere</a> but not the execution, and I pretty much hated <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9858517.All_These_Things_I_ve_Done__Birthright___1_' title='All These Things I've Done (Birthright, #1) by Gabrielle Zevin' rel='nofollow noopener'>All These Things I've Done</a>. But this book is just so warm and funny and bittersweet. It speaks to the thing inside me that has always loved books, will always love books, and has allowed my life to be swept in certain directions by my love for literatur</span>
  <span id="freeText15648484623870154382" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"There ain't nobody in the world like book people."</b>
</i><br /><br />It's a bit embarrassing to admit how emotional this book made me. I'm not even a fan of Zevin's work; I quite liked the concept behind <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/359410.Elsewhere" title="Elsewhere by Gabrielle Zevin" rel="nofollow noopener">Elsewhere</a> but not the execution, and I pretty much hated <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9858517.All_These_Things_I_ve_Done__Birthright___1_" title="All These Things I've Done (Birthright, #1) by Gabrielle Zevin" rel="nofollow noopener">All These Things I've Done</a>. But this book is just so warm and funny and bittersweet. It speaks to the thing inside me that has always loved books, will always love books, and has allowed my life to be swept in certain directions by my love for literature.<br /><br />A.J. Fikry is one of my favourite kinds of characters - he's cynical and grumpy, but simultaneously witty, clever, funny and lovable. This is essentially the tale of his life after the death of his beloved wife. He must somehow pick up the pieces of his world and continue managing his bookstore, while all he really wants to do is drink away his problems.<br /><br />One day, A.J. receives an unexpected package that is guaranteed to completely change his life. Like many great books, his life twists in a strange new direction, introducing him to new people and new ways of thinking. He soon begins to realise that he still has many things worth living for.<br /><br />Woven with allusions to many works of literature - especially short stories - this novel should resonate with many book lovers. Those of us who have been truly affected, influenced, changed or - dare I be so melodramatic - even <i>saved</i> by them. I don't know if Zevin intended to make a point about the death of the bookstore and physical books in favour of ereaders, but I found myself feeling a little melancholy as time went by and more people stopped buying physical books. Though ultimately relieved, as I realised how important bookstores and paper books still are to many people.<br /><br />Whether this book is for you or not, I cannot say. It is both funny and serious, happy and sad, light and dark... but I wouldn't have it any other way. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15648484623870154382" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_979039648" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/979039648" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/979039648?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=books-about-books-about-books">books-about-books-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=free-from-work">free-from-work</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer979039648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14089373421879775400"><i>A town isn't a town without a bookstore.</i><br/><br/>while it's true that this is the literary equivalent of a stone skipped over a pond, it's a pretty damn charming stone. reading about other booknerds, even when they are better described as bookcranks, is delightful to me. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7998632.A_Novel_Bookstore' title='A Novel Bookstore by Laurence Cossé' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Novel Bookstore</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/488447.Salamander' title='Salamander by Thomas Wharton' rel='nofollow noopener'>Salamander</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13538873.Mr__Penumbra_s_24_Hour_Bookstore__Mr__Penumbra_s_24_Hour_Bookstore___1_' title='Mr. Penumbra's 24-Hour Bookstore (Mr. Penumbra's 24-Hour Bookstore, #1) by Robin Sloan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mr. Penumbra's 24-Hour Bookstore</a>, etc are among my favorite books. are they the best books ever written? nah. but they have characters whose sensibilities are so close to my own, it's hard not to feel a lit</span>
  <span id="freeText14089373421879775400" style="display:none"><i>A town isn't a town without a bookstore.</i><br><br>while it's true that this is the literary equivalent of a stone skipped over a pond, it's a pretty damn charming stone. reading about other booknerds, even when they are better described as bookcranks, is delightful to me. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7998632.A_Novel_Bookstore" title="A Novel Bookstore by Laurence Cossé" rel="nofollow noopener">A Novel Bookstore</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/488447.Salamander" title="Salamander by Thomas Wharton" rel="nofollow noopener">Salamander</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13538873.Mr__Penumbra_s_24_Hour_Bookstore__Mr__Penumbra_s_24_Hour_Bookstore___1_" title="Mr. Penumbra's 24-Hour Bookstore (Mr. Penumbra's 24-Hour Bookstore, #1) by Robin Sloan" rel="nofollow noopener">Mr. Penumbra's 24-Hour Bookstore</a>, etc are among my favorite books. are they the best books ever written? nah. but they have characters whose sensibilities are so close to my own, it's hard not to feel a little heartswell when you encounter them. because if you're on goodreads at all, you know that books <i>matter</i>. whether you read the kinds of vampire books that fikry laments or the more serious tomes he applauds (although considering he esteems <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19063.The_Book_Thief" title="The Book Thief by Markus Zusak" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Thief</a>, hasn't finished proust's ISOLT, and dismisses <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6759.Infinite_Jest" title="Infinite Jest by David Foster Wallace" rel="nofollow noopener">Infinite Jest</a>, i'm taking his purported book-snobbery with a grain of salt), you know the power of a good story, even when it's just a sweet little piece of light escapism.<br><br>this is a love letter to booklovers about the power of the written word to bring people together whether the relationships be romantic, parental, or book-clubby.<br><br>several of these relationships involve the titular a.j. fikry; a bookstore owner and widower living on a small island somewhere new england-y who finds himself entrusted with the care of a two-year-old named maya after she is abandoned in his bookstore. he's already old-man curmudgeonly although still in his thirties, but finds the raising of maya and instilling in her his own love of books to be one of those rewarding experiences that enriches one's life and is all sorts of inspirational. although he expresses it differently.<br><br><i><b>Fucking love,</b> he thinks. <b>What a bother.</b> It's completely gotten in the way of his plan to drink himself to death, to drive his business to ruin. The most annoying thing about it is that once a person gives a shit about one thing, he finds he has to start giving a shit about everything.</i><br><br>and give a shit he does, as his love for maya allows him to nurture other feelings including reluctantly acknowledged romantic ones for a vibrant book-loving woman with her own relationship baggage. in a comment that sounds like something ripped right out of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2175.Madame_Bovary" title="Madame Bovary by Gustave Flaubert" rel="nofollow noopener">Madame Bovary</a>,<br><br><i>Her mother likes to say that novels have ruined Amelia for real men.</i><br><br>thankfully for fikry, this is not true, because he is indeed a real, flawed man. <br><br>but he's also the kind of man whose first-date chatter involves "In what restaurant based on a novel would you have preferred to dine*?"<br><br>so he's got some good points. <br><br>so it's a romance and a sort-of cozy mystery (although the theft of his copy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22895415.Tamerlane_Poem" title="Tamerlane Poem by Edgar Allan Poe" rel="nofollow noopener">Tamerlane: Poem</a> is not important to the story - until it is), and one of those cheeky feel-good smalltown books in which suicides both occur and are contemplated and people die and there are miscarriages and infidelity, but it's all glossed over in the same way as those other pesky realities like how an abandoned-child scenario would really be handled. because, no.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434740923i/15258000._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>so despite the supremely precocious maya and the novel's relentlessly cheerful tone, both of which i would ordinarily find irritating, i enjoyed the bookyness of it more than i was irritated by its greeting card outlook. all the discussions about the perils of e-books and chain bookstores (<i>the only thing worse than a world with big chain bookstores was a world with NO big chain bookstores.</i>),the methods of publishing reps, the assessment that blurbs are <i>the blood diamonds of publishing</i>, "nerd" as a term of endearment, all the meta stuff at the beginning "if this were a book…." - it's all stuff from "my" world, so it's easy to love. <br><br>it's a very quick read about bookfolk that may not be the most cerebral thing on the shelves, but it's hard not to get caught up in its genuine enthusiasm and start nodding along nerdily at certain moments.<br><br>it's summer- enjoy yourself.<br><br>* my answer - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6689.James_and_the_Giant_Peach" title="James and the Giant Peach by Roald Dahl" rel="nofollow noopener">James and the Giant Peach</a>. with giant animatronic bugs, slightly scarier than the ones on the film, and a menu including<br><br>baked peaches with ricotta and honey<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434740923i/15258001._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>chicken with peach chutney<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434740923i/15258002.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>peach cobbler<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434740923i/15258003.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>peach crisp<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434740923i/15258004._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>peach and pancetta pizza<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434740923i/15258005.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>peach soup<br><br><img <div id="review_2399948976" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2399948976" />
    <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister"><img alt="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486056026p2/4971692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2399948976?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister">Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=seriously-funny">seriously-funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=sweet">sweet</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2399948976" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15054296749425093927"><b>*4.5 Stars* — because how can any bonafide book-nerd <i>not</i> adore this quirky and heartfelt tribute to literature!</b><br/><br/>I don’t know about you, but I could dwell inside the richly entertaining mind of one <b>
  <i>A.J. Fickry</i>
</b> forever. Or at least every other weekend. <br/><br/>Because that’s exactly what this novel simulates: a casual stroll through the mind of a complex, yet vastly simple middle-aged widower whose outlook on life has deflated. <br/><br/> Life has knocked him down, as it tends to do, and A.J. finds comfort in th</span>
  <span id="freeText15054296749425093927" style="display:none"><b>*4.5 Stars* — because how can any bonafide book-nerd <i>not</i> adore this quirky and heartfelt tribute to literature!</b><br /><br />I don’t know about you, but I could dwell inside the richly entertaining mind of one <b>
  <i>A.J. Fickry</i>
</b> forever. Or at least every other weekend. <br /><br />Because that’s exactly what this novel simulates: a casual stroll through the mind of a complex, yet vastly simple middle-aged widower whose outlook on life has deflated. <br /><br /> Life has knocked him down, as it tends to do, and A.J. finds comfort in the cold embrace of pessimism and gloom…And, of course, in his ownership of the town’s one and only <b>bookstore.</b><br /><br />But a mysterious “package” popping up in his store will spark a powerful change in A.J., and even the townspeople, who typically view him as a grouchy ol’ book-snob will take notice. <br /><br />The heart of this story explores the process of grief and the regaining of hope—but in a very gentle manner. The tragedies, although deep, are not pronounced within its writing. <br /><br />This plot mimics life in the way that it keeps moving forward. And despite the fact that its reader will likely be moved to tears, the next chapter follows, bringing with it the inevitable “new day” whether you’re ready for it or not. <br /><br />Along with the side-effects of heartache, this author infuses generous amounts humor, a wholesome romance, and a sprinkle of mystery within these pages. A.J.’s selective taste for quality literature is endearing, and his judgments of the rest of the book world—comical. <br /><br />I loved the various references to classics, and how each chapter begins with the mention of one—A.J.’s unique perspective included. He often views the people in his world as characters in a book, predicting their next move based off his astute knowledge of fictional-being-behavior. <br /><br />The more I think about it, the more this book just seems <i>so</i> incredibly <b>simple</b>, yet has hit me with such surprising force that I can still feel it buzzing. I’ve claimed more times than I can count how I’ll “never forget” a book. But time passes, and only a select few truly stand out. I think this will be one of those few. <br /><br /><b><u>Just some of my favorite A.J. quotes</u>:</b><br /><i>”What a stupid melodramatic thing for her to do. What a goddamn Danielle Steel move, Nic! If this were a novel, I’d stop reading right now. I’d throw it across the room.”<br /><br />“You know everything you need to know about a person from the answer to the question, what is your favorite book?”<br /><br />“Someday, you may think of marrying. Pick someone who thinks you're the only person in the room.”<br /><br />“We read to know we’re not alone. We read because we are alone. We read and we are not alone. We are not alone.</i><br /><br /><i>*Shout out to Crumb, whose enthusiastic review of this one made me rush to purchase on amazon!*</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15054296749425093927" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText9663732568537404759" style="display:none">What can I say?<br>This novel was the ruination of me.. and I couldn't be happier. Sometimes when i love a book to pieces, it is easy to write a review and sometimes it is difficult. For this novel, the latter is true. I lack the adequate language needed to evoke the emotion that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18293427.The_Storied_Life_of_A_J__Fikry" title="The Storied Life of A.J. Fikry by Gabrielle Zevin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Storied Life of A.J. Fikry</a> stirred within me. You can't help but fall in love with the curmudgeon, bookseller A.J. I don't know if I've ever loved a character more than him. Although the plot was simplistic, the subtleties and intricacies of the characterization were not. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/40593.Gabrielle_Zevin" title="Gabrielle Zevin" rel="nofollow noopener">Gabrielle Zevin</a> used nuanced language to describe the character relationships. She is a masterful storyteller and is not just a writer, she is an artist. She blew life into her characters and made them come alive on the pages. If you consider yourself a book lover..<br><b>I dare you not to fall in love with this book.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1526645328ra/25561625.gif" width="400" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_933693512" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/933693512" />
    <a title="Carmen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen"><img alt="Carmen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412617445p2/25353295.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/933693512?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmen" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen">Carmen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781616204518" href="/book/show/20312470-the-storied-life-of-a-j-fikry">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of John Green and Nicholas Sparks</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=traditionally-published">traditionally-published</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=she-says">she-says</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=american-author">american-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=published2014">published2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer933693512" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7423952149615694860">This is the most precious, adorable, cutesy-wootsey bunch of tripe I have ever read in my life. How is this book so popular? It's cliché after cliché after cliché ad nauseam. Ugh.<br/><br/>A grumpy-grumpy bookseller who is a widower leads a sad and lonely Scrooge-like life until a chubby, perfect, articulate, beautiful baby is left in his book shop and teaches him to love and live again! Excuse me while I go vomit in the corner. Then to top it all off <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[he gets brain cancer and his loving (ne</span></span>
  <span id="freeText7423952149615694860" style="display:none">This is the most precious, adorable, cutesy-wootsey bunch of tripe I have ever read in my life. How is this book so popular? It's cliché after cliché after cliché ad nauseam. Ugh.<br /><br />A grumpy-grumpy bookseller who is a widower leads a sad and lonely Scrooge-like life until a chubby, perfect, articulate, beautiful baby is left in his book shop and teaches him to love and live again! Excuse me while I go vomit in the corner. Then to top it all off <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[he gets brain cancer and his loving (new) wife and (adopted) daughter sob and watch their loved one pass away while he babbles about stuff like "Life is only about love" and crap like that. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Don't read this unless you want extremely predictable, emotionally manipulative schmaltz. Every character has the same kind of perky, intelligent, isn't-life-cute? voice. Everything is made "cute." Cute suicide, cute violent sudden death, cute <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[cancer <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, cute baby abandonment, cute heartlessness, cute infidelity, cute alcoholism.<br /><br />Nothing exists in life that is not adorable, apparently.<br /><br />People seem to love this book for either two reasons:<br />1.) They want an uplifting, cutesy book about how everything in life happens for a <i>reason</i>, and aren't people and all their quirks just adorable?!?<br /><br />2.) They like talking about books, reading about books, reading books about books, listening to people spout on about books.<br /><br />Look, I get it, I understand. I love talking about books, too. It's why I joined GR. But I just couldn't take this constant book-loving masturbatory exercise which is like a never-ending stream of BOOKS ARE THE BEST AND MOST IMPORTANT THINGS IN LIFE. I love books, I read every day, but I like to read books that are about stuff like life and people. I haven't really reached the meta point of wanting to read books that are about books and just constant praise of books.<br /><br />Tl;dr - Predictable, schmaltzy tripe that serves no purpose except to offer a fluffy escape from life (which sometimes you need, I'll admit) OR a book-loving masturbatory session where you can think about books and squee over books WHILE reading a book. Not my cup of tea. Two stars and not one because it's cute and made me laugh three times. Also, bonus points for having the two MCs be non-white.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7423952149615694860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1850138104" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1850138104?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Always Pouting" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Always Pouting" href="/user/show/48650982-always-pouting">Always Pouting</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/21445677-the-storied-life-of-a-j-fikry">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1850138104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11983393630440586249">I wanted to like this book, the writing was good and the characters were interesting but I just couldn't. I know that A.J. is the one being critical and snobbish about what entails good writing or literature but it just felt like I was being lectured to and god I resent being told what to do so much, also I think short stories are rarely good so I want to fight A.J. At one point also there's this passage about how if you see something mentioned in the beginning of the book you want it to come ba</span>
  <span id="freeText11983393630440586249" style="display:none">I wanted to like this book, the writing was good and the characters were interesting but I just couldn't. I know that A.J. is the one being critical and snobbish about what entails good writing or literature but it just felt like I was being lectured to and god I resent being told what to do so much, also I think short stories are rarely good so I want to fight A.J. At one point also there's this passage about how if you see something mentioned in the beginning of the book you want it to come back at the end and play a part out and then that happens in the story itself with a lot of things and it didn't seem like cute and self aware but again it just came off as the author patting themselves on the back for how much they know about writing. How am I supposed to get into the story when the author keeps jarring me away from it by talking about things like that man. Also for someone who makes a good chunk of the book be about what makes a book or story good, the author seems not to have developed the story she was writing that well. I don't think we needed to follow A.J. for so many years the way the story does and towards the end the story started to get kind of flat. I know the author was trying to be clever with the plot and usually I like when everything comes back full circle but I just don't think it worked here. The writing was good and the characters and premise interesting and I wish it had been written differently so we only got the story for those few days before he gets left with Maya or something. I don't know I feel like I could've enjoyed this more if it was just structured different or something and I don't get why at the end that thing happens to AJ like was that necessary...<br /><br /><br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_900539630" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900539630" />

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/900539630?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ann" href="/user/show/985163-ann">Ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781616203948" href="/book/show/20794246-the-storied-life-of-a-j-fikry">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/985163-ann?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/985163-ann?shelf=family-relationships">family-relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/985163-ann?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/985163-ann?shelf=small-business">small-business</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/985163-ann?shelf=new-england">new-england</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/985163-ann?shelf=adoption-foster-system">adoption-foster-system</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/985163-ann?shelf=marriage">marriage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/985163-ann?shelf=massachusetts">massachusetts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/985163-ann?shelf=widows-widowers">widows-widowers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/985163-ann?shelf=country-small-town">country-small-town</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer900539630" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4537682045094738748">Thank you to the publisher for an advance reading copy.<br/><br/>I shouldn't have read this. A book marketed as "heartwarming" is never for me. But I read it anyway because I love books about books so much, and it sounded so good! Based on the book's description and marketing, I know that it's meant to really appeal to book clubs and librarians and bookstores, and I think the author is doing everything humanly possible to kiss up to those groups without delivering anything with any depth. I don't think it</span>
  <span id="freeText4537682045094738748" style="display:none">Thank you to the publisher for an advance reading copy.<br /><br />I shouldn't have read this. A book marketed as "heartwarming" is never for me. But I read it anyway because I love books about books so much, and it sounded so good! Based on the book's description and marketing, I know that it's meant to really appeal to book clubs and librarians and bookstores, and I think the author is doing everything humanly possible to kiss up to those groups without delivering anything with any depth. I don't think it necessarily has to be literary, but the story is told in a completely shallow way and is spread unbelievably thin, which renders the message pretty meaningless. The author is trying <i>so</i> hard to be cute and clever, and I rolled my eyes over and over again because it all felt so calculated to be gobbled up by book lovers. I know she can write some really lovely things since some of the quotes from fictional books were wonderful. She would have made better use of her efforts to concentrate on that kind of writing style. (I also thought that it was funny that a book that talked about the importance carefully chosen language had so much filler; the <i>Book Thief</i> exchange was mindbogglingly unnecessary, and that was one of many). <br /><br />I believe that there are heartwarming books out there that can touch my cold black vortex of a heart. But this is insanely overhyped fluff, and I'm shocked that it's getting this much buzz. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4537682045094738748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_801555022" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/801555022" />
    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1166663-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1277905205p2/1166663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/801555022?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/1166663-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer801555022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8855317083966673635">There's joy in my heart and a skip in my step today after closing the last page of this jewel of a book. A must for book lovers and booksellers alike, <i>The Storied Life of A.J. Fikry</i> is an affirmation of the love of books and reading and how they meld lives together. <br/><br/>A.J. Fikry, is the owner of the independent bookstore, Island Books. Fikry is grieving the loss of his wife, sales are down, a rare book worth scads of money is stolen from the shop leaving him irritable, and irritating. Frankly he's</span>
  <span id="freeText8855317083966673635" style="display:none">There's joy in my heart and a skip in my step today after closing the last page of this jewel of a book. A must for book lovers and booksellers alike, <i>The Storied Life of A.J. Fikry</i> is an affirmation of the love of books and reading and how they meld lives together. <br /><br />A.J. Fikry, is the owner of the independent bookstore, Island Books. Fikry is grieving the loss of his wife, sales are down, a rare book worth scads of money is stolen from the shop leaving him irritable, and irritating. Frankly he's depressed and is turning more and more inward, cutting himself off more than the normal isolation of Alice Island living. Fate or something else entirely steps in when one night he finds a special package on his bookshop floor changing his life forever. <br /><br />Gabrielle Zevon treats us to some of the most likeable, memorable characters I've met in a long time. Though I adore them all, even cranky Fikry, my favorite is the cop, Lambiase, who in the line of duty must visit the store frequently and so buys books. Not wanting to waste his hard earned money, he reads the books and eventually leads the Chief's Choice Book Club. <br /><br />A question asked as part of A.J.F's reviews that head each chapter<br /> <i>"Is a twist less satisfying if you know it's coming?"</i><br />My answer, <i>"No A.J., No Gabrielle!"</i><br /><br />If you've ever wondered about the inner workings of an independent bookstore or how it might feel to be a sales rep pitching a publisher's catalog, put this on your list. If you like a feel good, romantic story that will make you smile with a need for a few tissues, put this on your list. <br /><br />To give credit where credit is due, my sincere thanks to Michael Rockliff of Workman Publishing for his spirited recommendation of <i>The Storied Life of A.J. Fikry</i> (April 2014) which sent me flying to Edelweiss to snag an advance copy. A nod to Algonquin for their trust in allowing me this reading experience.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8855317083966673635" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12844857837223124296">☺️☺️☺️☺️<br/><br/>This was really lovely. It was perfectly written (seriously, Gabrielle Zevin has mastered using the English language), and heartfelt. It was a little sappy at times, but it felt appropriate. I loved the span of this book - over a decade of fascinating stuff happened. And I loved the setting - a book store on a tiny island. I loved the emphasis on books and love and trying to be a good person. <br/><br/>I'm not giving a 5/5 simply because I don't think it did anything particularly new, and didn't m</span>
  <span id="freeText12844857837223124296" style="display:none">☺️☺️☺️☺️<br /><br />This was really lovely. It was perfectly written (seriously, Gabrielle Zevin has mastered using the English language), and heartfelt. It was a little sappy at times, but it felt appropriate. I loved the span of this book - over a decade of fascinating stuff happened. And I loved the setting - a book store on a tiny island. I loved the emphasis on books and love and trying to be a good person. <br /><br />I'm not giving a 5/5 simply because I don't think it did anything particularly new, and didn't make me think about something I'd never thought about before. That's okay, and it doesn't make this book in anyway bad, but it didn't leave me blown away and so four stars it is.</span>

<div id="review_1178057923" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1178057923" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1178057923?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=book-club-reads">book-club-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=library-has">library-has</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1178057923" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15265736661398626384">It's entirely possible that I'm as much of a curmudgeon as A.J. Fikry. <br/><br/>Reading a book about a bookstore and books and the people who love them seemed like a can't-miss proposition. And, in fact, there were parts of this book that I liked very much: the police chief who unexpectedly turns himself and most of his force into readers; the subplot with the theft of Poe's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22895415.Tamerlane_Poem' title='Tamerlane Poem by Edgar Allan Poe' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tamerlane: Poem</a>; the brief chapter intros where A.J. talks about various stories. <br/><br/>But overall the novel just felt a lot more superf</span>
  <span id="freeText15265736661398626384" style="display:none">It's entirely possible that I'm as much of a curmudgeon as A.J. Fikry. <br /><br />Reading a book about a bookstore and books and the people who love them seemed like a can't-miss proposition. And, in fact, there were parts of this book that I liked very much: the police chief who unexpectedly turns himself and most of his force into readers; the subplot with the theft of Poe's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22895415.Tamerlane_Poem" title="Tamerlane Poem by Edgar Allan Poe" rel="nofollow noopener">Tamerlane: Poem</a>; the brief chapter intros where A.J. talks about various stories. <br /><br />But overall the novel just felt a lot more superficial and clichéd than I was expecting or hoping. And then the ending doubled down on the sentimentalism with an overused trope (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[death of a main character from cancer <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>).<br /><br />I'll confess that I'm a person who cries way too easily in sentimental scenes in movies or books. (One of the more embarrassing moments of my life was when I was on a date and we were watching one of those silly old Arnold Schwarzenegger <i>Conan the Barbarian</i> movies and laughing about how dumb it was, and then the girl dies and Conan is sad and I start to leak tears, hiding my face from my date because I was so mortified that I was crying over this idiotic movie). Just so you know this is coming from someone who easily gets sucked in by sentimentalism. But the ending of this book? Didn't move me in the slightest. I was just mildly annoyed at the over-familiar direction the plot took.<br /><br />Still, there were some good moments and several delightful scenes, like this description of the book club started by Police Chief Lambiase:<blockquote>Years ago, Lambiase had had to institute a "leave your weapons" policy after a young cop had pulled a gun on another cop during a particularly heated discussion of <i>The House of Sand and Fog</i>. (Lambiase would later reflect to A.J. that the selection had been a mistake. "Had an interesting cop character but too much moral ambiguity in that one. I'm going to stick to easier genre stuff from now on.")</blockquote>3.5 stars.<br /><br />Content notes: a handful of F-bombs and some characters sleeping together, but nothing explicit.</span>

<div id="review_894756529" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/894756529" />
    <a title="Diane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/279256-diane"><img alt="Diane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1497365060p2/279256.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/894756529?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane" href="/user/show/279256-diane">Diane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/279256-diane?shelf=grumpy-old-man">grumpy-old-man</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/279256-diane?shelf=bookishness">bookishness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer894756529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17813701626060334659">This is not a perfect novel, but it is filled with bookish charm and easy grace. <br/><br/>I picked up <i>The Storied Life of A.J. Fikry</i> at just the right time. I wanted something light and entertaining, and (hopefully) with a happy ending. And that is what I got, with the bonus of lots of literary references, some small-town whimsy and even a little romance.<br/><br/>A. J. Fikry is a cranky bookstore owner in New England. His life is in a rut: He lost his wife, his store is struggling and then his rare copy of Edgar </span>
  <span id="freeText17813701626060334659" style="display:none">This is not a perfect novel, but it is filled with bookish charm and easy grace. <br /><br />I picked up <i>The Storied Life of A.J. Fikry</i> at just the right time. I wanted something light and entertaining, and (hopefully) with a happy ending. And that is what I got, with the bonus of lots of literary references, some small-town whimsy and even a little romance.<br /><br />A. J. Fikry is a cranky bookstore owner in New England. His life is in a rut: He lost his wife, his store is struggling and then his rare copy of Edgar Allen Poe poems is stolen. His fortunes change when a precocious child is abandoned in his store, and Fikry surprises everyone in the town by deciding to adopt her.<br /><br />While the plot is formulaic — Grouchy Man Finds Love! — what kicked it into the Charming category were its fun bookish comments. Fikry is a man who has lots of opinions about books. Check out this rant he delivers to a publisher's sales rep:<br /><br /><blockquote> <br />"I do not like postmodernism, postapocalyptic settings, postmortem narrators, or magic realism. I rarely respond to supposedly clever formal devices, multiple fonts, pictures where they shouldn't be -- basically, gimmicks of any kind. I find literary fiction about the Holocaust or any other major world tragedy to be distasteful -- nonfiction only, please. I do not like genre mash-ups a la the literary detective novel or the literary fantasy. Literary should be literary, and genre should be genre, and crossbreeding rarely results in anything satisfying. I do not like children's books, especially ones with orphans, and I prefer not to clutter my shelves with young adult. I do not like anything over four hundred pages or under one hundred fifty pages. I am repulsed by ghostwritten novels by reality television stars, celebrity pictures books, sports memoirs, movie tie-in editions, novelty items, and — I imagined this goes without saying — vampires. I rarely stock debuts, chick lit, poetry, or translations. I would prefer not to stock series, but the demands of my pocketbook require me to. For your part, you needn't tell me about the 'next big series' until it is ensconced on the New York Times Best Sellers list."<br /></blockquote><br /><br />Hahaha! While I agree with some but not all of that speech, the point is that I enjoy characters who themselves are well-read and literary. Fikry lists different authors and stories throughout the book, and I'm excited to go look up those I have not yet read.<br /><br />The book has some good bookish quotes and your usual colorful cast of small-town characters. This is a pleasant, entertaining novel and was perfect for summer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17813701626060334659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
