  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3450578043" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3450578043" />
    <a title="Merphy Napier" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41973734-merphy-napier"><img alt="Merphy Napier" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524921716p2/41973734.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3450578043?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Merphy Napier" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Merphy Napier" href="/user/show/41973734-merphy-napier">Merphy Napier</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41973734-merphy-napier?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41973734-merphy-napier?shelf=two-stars">two-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41973734-merphy-napier?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3450578043" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6442555089971637149">I'll start off by saying this isn't a bad book so I don't want to discourage people from reading it. It just did so many things that I didn't like. <br/><br/>What I did like:<br/>- The writing is beautiful. Zevin had thoughtful prose and she had that slow, personal pacing that my favorite author, Fredrick Backmen has in his books. <br/>- The characters were easy to fall in love with from the start, despite their (intentional) flaws. Getting invested in these characters and their stories was not difficult for me at </span>
  <span id="freeText6442555089971637149" style="display:none">I'll start off by saying this isn't a bad book so I don't want to discourage people from reading it. It just did so many things that I didn't like. <br /><br />What I did like:<br />- The writing is beautiful. Zevin had thoughtful prose and she had that slow, personal pacing that my favorite author, Fredrick Backmen has in his books. <br />- The characters were easy to fall in love with from the start, despite their (intentional) flaws. Getting invested in these characters and their stories was not difficult for me at all.<br />- The last page. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the fact that it ends by saying the same thing that was in the beginning, "the book seller won't take what he can't sell" and then we walk in to that last line, showing us that his friend took over this bookstore. That was beautiful  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />What I didn't like:<br /><br />Unfortunately, the at the halfway point things started going downhill for me. I'll start with a nitpick and work my way down.<br /><br />- rushed moments. This was actually in the first half. Stuff like <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The officer agreeing to let Fikry take the two year old home with him and it's all just accepted and brushed over. So the officer didn't call any families that would be more equipped? No paperwork was filled out? He didn't even care that Fikry is driving this two year old around without a carseat????? No carseat is fine with him?! I went back and double checked, none was ever mentioned when he was driving or when she was left in his store. This could have been easily resolved if it were just written out rather than rushing through it. Same with the adoption. Just a couple of really quick lines like, "There were a few things counting against me, but it worked out. The adoption took the normal amount of time." then goes on to say it took less than a year. As someone currently going through the adoption process, no, it doesn't take under a year. The "normal amount of time" is closer to 2-4 years (even several years ago when this was set). I would have loved a bit of a look into the adoption rather than just rushing through it. Again, it's a nit pic, but there are several more scenes I could write here that were just rushed through or brushed over and I felt it took authenticity from the experience.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />- Tonal shift. At about the halfway point, we move on from a story about a grump of a man who is figuring out how to raise his new daughter (which was really sweet), to a grump of a man trying to win over the woman he's falling for. It's fine, I get that some people will like this section, I just didn't like the shift.<br /><br />Now we get to the part that I really hated. And that's the last quarter of the book.<br /><br />- The twist (for lack of better word) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Cancer. Why does it ALWAYS have to be Cancer? I knew this was coming back because he had that strong reaction to the book about Cancer, then very shortly after, he stated that he believes in the principal of Chekhov's gun, so I knew the gun had to come back in act three. But I really hated how it came back. I thought a lot about this. Why can authors like Backmen write about topics very personal and painful to me and I feel seen, but other authors write it and I feel like it was used as a cheep device and it makes me mad? I think the reason is that some authors (like Backmen) write it in a raw and emotional way where we dig deep into the realities of it together, where as others feel like "They have Cancer. Now they're dead. Now cry. End book." When there's little exploration of the emotions and the reality of it and it's just a quick reveal, followed by an emotional scene, then end... ug. I get what the author was trying to do, but I don't think it was done well. It was a "hit 'em with emotion and leave 'em" and I just really don't like that.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />- the plot device. It was so convoluted and ridiculous and what was the point in the end? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The book. I knew this had to come back eventually too. Of course it did. But when we get to how it comes back and the explanation, it was so convoluted! I mean, "I stole the book then gave it to this person to pay them off, then she came back two years later and said she couldn't sell it so she just gave it back to me, so I just put it in my closet for years, then this guy came over for the first time and saw it and knew what it was but didn't say anything, then years later after we were married, when it was needed the most, he confronted me and THEN we gave it back to him in a way so he would never find out who stole it from him in the first place." So, Fikry needed a surgery he couldn't afford to give him a couple more years to live, and now that Fikry has the book back, he can sell it and afford the surgery. Yay! He gets a few more years to live! So we just jumped through a bunch of hoops to makes sense of this book ring-a-round so we can go through this whole story, *only to skip that part of his life*. No joke, we went through all that to give Fikry a couple more years to live, then we skip over those extra years and get right to his death. Only adding to how this felt like a gimmick to me, not an exploration of a deep topic. We're not focused on his life anymore, the extra life we went through all that to get, we don't even see. Skip straight to the death and end book. So what was the point of the book plot of it doesn't even effect how we get the story?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Again, a lot of people love this book, and I get it. It's well written and it's an emotional book. For me, I felt like I get what the author was trying to do, but I didn't like her execution of it at all. I'm gonna go read "A Man Called Ove" to make myself feel better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6442555089971637149" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11855391111364435621" style="display:none">SOS.<br /><br />HELP. <br /><br />THE SITUATION IS DIRE.<br /><br />I can’t stop reading books about bookstores.<br /><br />A book about a bookworm will do in a pinch, but really bookstores are the only way to go. And it’s gotten so grim that I’ve resorted to rereading books I read a few years ago and vaguely remember being pretty good but had no intention of rereading.<br /><br />Luckily, in this case, it turned out to be better than pretty good.<br /><br />I read this in between a couple of romancey fluffy things about bookstores, which really were more vessels for two people making gushy eye contact with each other over 300 pages than any sort of bibliophilia.<br /><br />This had a good amount of both of those things, which is a compromise I can live with. Mostly because it had significantly more bookishness than lovey dovey gushiness. And I’m in it for the bookstores, after all.<br /><br />This is also refreshing because...not all of the gushiness and emotions are romantic?? Far from it, actually. Lots of found family stuff going on here and that is always good in my book. (Get it? Good in MY BOOK? Like, it’s always good in the book that I’m reading? Ah, we have fun.)<br /><br />This isn’t exactly life changing, or anything, and I won’t think about it often (as opposed to books I five star, which I think about for 45 minutes each and every day), but it is sweet and nice and bookish.<br /><br />What more could you want?!<br /><br />Bottom line: Yippee! (Don’t think I’ve ever used that word before and I’m already regretting it now.)<br /><br />-------------<br /><br />this was a complete delight.<br /><br />review to come / 4.5 stars (for now)<br /><br />-------------<br /><br />i think if i only read books about bookstores for the rest of my life i'd be okay with that</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1176683941" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1176683941?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35906603-the-storied-life-of-a-j-fikry">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=favs-of-2018">favs-of-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1176683941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12542178365544124673">When people would say, "Every book lover needs to read this book," I always thought it was such a stupid basis to recommend a book off of. Just because a book breaks a fourth wall and presents a story about a fellow book lover doesn't mean it's better than any other book out there. But after reading this book, I get it. I get it so much. This book is for every book lover. And I will never shame someone for recommending it on that front ever again. This story will truly connect to people who live</span>
  <span id="freeText12542178365544124673" style="display:none">When people would say, "Every book lover needs to read this book," I always thought it was such a stupid basis to recommend a book off of. Just because a book breaks a fourth wall and presents a story about a fellow book lover doesn't mean it's better than any other book out there. But after reading this book, I get it. I get it so much. This book is for every book lover. And I will never shame someone for recommending it on that front ever again. This story will truly connect to people who live and breathe books, much like the characters themselves. Even though I was like none of these characters, I saw myself in them nevertheless just because of our shared passion for literature.<br /><br />This is another one of those books that has emotional parts to it but I don't ever cry until I finish it and close the book and the weight of it finally descends upon me. It's not a heavy story, but it's just so phenomenally done. It reads with the simplicity of a short story but still carries its own weight throughout the progression of the entire lifetime of its characters. And the characters were the best part about this--SO many threads came together and not one detail goes unwoven somewhere into this story. Nothing is meaningless. I loathe this book for how much I wish I could write like it.<br /><br />I anticipate this book will be sticking with me for a long time. It was so heartfelt and although I questioned if it's truly deserving of 5 stars, the sheer structure of this and the mastery of connecting every little detail together was so precise, I had to give it the credit it deserves.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12542178365544124673" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15590910811974200701">3.5 stars<br/><br/>This is a story to be read solely for the nerdistic cachet of getting all the literary references and book biz jokes. Even if you're alone and there's no one to applaud you for being so well read, there's still that little frisson of snobbish self-satisfaction when you recognize the book or short story mentioned or alluded to. <i>And</i> when you know which books and authors are made up, because you've never heard of them. Am I really that much of a book dork that I give a rodent's posterior a</span>
  <span id="freeText15590910811974200701" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />This is a story to be read solely for the nerdistic cachet of getting all the literary references and book biz jokes. Even if you're alone and there's no one to applaud you for being so well read, there's still that little frisson of snobbish self-satisfaction when you recognize the book or short story mentioned or alluded to. <i>And</i> when you know which books and authors are made up, because you've never heard of them. Am I really that much of a book dork that I give a rodent's posterior about such trivia? Why yes. Yes I am. And if you're not that dorky, reading this book might make you wish you were more like us, the beautiful people. The special ones. The winners. No, only kidding. My NPD is showing. <br /><br /> </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer904077083" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12612204228897317783">Don't you just love reading a book that you can't wait to get back to, a book you want to savour yet <i>must</i> keep on reading. This <i>UNPUTDOWNABLE</i> delightful story about a charming little bookstore (and so much more) fit into that category for me. It combines laugh-out-loud moments with an occasional need for a tissue, engaging characters with real life problems and a twist or two along the way.<p>Another 2014 favorite for this book lover!</p><p>
  <i>(It pains me that we are losing our beloved bookstores. I do e</i></p></span>
  <span id="freeText12612204228897317783" style="display:none">Don't you just love reading a book that you can't wait to get back to, a book you want to savour yet <i>must</i> keep on reading. This <i>UNPUTDOWNABLE</i> delightful story about a charming little bookstore (and so much more) fit into that category for me. It combines laugh-out-loud moments with an occasional need for a tissue, engaging characters with real life problems and a twist or two along the way.<p>Another 2014 favorite for this book lover!</p><p>

<div id="review_998462955" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/998462955" />
    <a title="Debbie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8665845-debbie"><img alt="Debbie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334166735p2/8665845.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/998462955?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie" href="/user/show/8665845-debbie">Debbie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/21937305-the-storied-life-of-a-j-fikry">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=best-reads-2012-through-2019">best-reads-2012-through-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer998462955" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13026516594009435025">A friend’s 7-year-old daughter once told her, “Mom, you need a trip to paradise.” I wish my kid had said it to me, but never mind. I’m taking it to mean, “Mom, you <i>and Debbie</i> need a trip to paradise.” Well, holy shit, I found it! Island Books, the setting for this book, is located smack in the middle of paradise.<br/><br/>I purposely didn’t read any reviews before diving in, and I’m glad. Strange and wonderful things start happening right from the beginning, and I’m caught off guard and delighted. I thoug</span>
  <span id="freeText13026516594009435025" style="display:none">A friend’s 7-year-old daughter once told her, “Mom, you need a trip to paradise.” I wish my kid had said it to me, but never mind. I’m taking it to mean, “Mom, you <i>and Debbie</i> need a trip to paradise.” Well, holy shit, I found it! Island Books, the setting for this book, is located smack in the middle of paradise.<br /><br />I purposely didn’t read any reviews before diving in, and I’m glad. Strange and wonderful things start happening right from the beginning, and I’m caught off guard and delighted. I thought, oh this is a great author—she knows how to keep the action going lickety-split, and she knows that it works to throw in things that are unexpected. I’ll avoid talking about the actual plot line in the hope that you get the same element of surprise that I did. I’ll only say it’s about a guy who owns a bookstore. If you can, try to avoid reviews that summarize what happens.<br /> <br />I didn’t want it to be over. Okay, it’s cool enough that the book is about a bookstore, but there are tons of other book goodies. First and foremost, you get to hang out with a bunch of other book nuts. That’s cathartic in itself. And there are, naturally, book recommendations that make you want a grab a pencil and write them down. But that’s just the tip of the iceberg. Want to read a kid’s short story? And attend the short story competition? Want to go to an exciting and bizarre author signing? Want to live above a bookstore? Want to join a book club? Want a few nuggets on writing? But wait, there’s more. There’s a book theft. There’s a publishing company rep pushing titles. And every chapter opens with a reference to a literary work, followed by tender and thoughtful comments about it.<br /> <br />It’s like the author said to herself, hm….what would a book lover salivate over? And she nails it. Think about every permutation of book lust, and it’s here. It’s like crack to all us book addicts. And what a fix we get!<br /> <br />I wasn’t sure going into this one. Will the tone be lecture-y? Will the book titles be esoteric? The answer to both better be no, or I’ll be annoyed big time—though in fact my bristly annoyance would simply be covering up my insecurity about being unread and stupid.<br /> <br />I needn’t have worried. I knew some of the titles, but not all, but I never felt like I was in trouble for not recognizing some of them. Besides, when I go to a bookstore, I’m not going to recognize all the titles, or kick myself for not knowing them. And the author is gentle about it—she creates a main character who is realistic and kind; who talks about books in a way that’s inviting and playful, not arrogant or pedantic. Because his livelihood depends on his selling books, and because he’s basically a nice guy, he’s never condescending to his buyers. He wants to sell books, yes, but he also wants to share his book lust and help people find nirvana through books.<br /><br />This genius author makes sure the book talk never overpowers the plot; it only enhances it. And there is so much more here. There are a couple of juicy mysteries, and I didn’t have a clue how they’d be solved—but they are wrapped up nicely. There’s humor, romance, pathos, suspense, and a lot of “feel good” (without being all Hallmarky). The characters are engaging: well-drawn, complex, quirky, and sympathetic. The author weaves a really good yarn that flows at a great pace; there are no side trips down the alleys of philosophy or history.<br /><br />As an ex-editor, I found a couple of minute logistical issues—probably too small to even mention, but with my editor OCD, I must. (Help me stop doing this, please!) The funniest instance was when the main character went to a bar in his underwear and bathrobe—the author just forgot to somehow get him back home so he could get dressed before heading to the bar.<br /> <br />And one more thing, which is not so minute, but which I didn’t care about because I was so sold on this book already: The young kid speaks like an adult. And it was so disconcerting, I repeatedly tried to pinpoint her age, which really was unnecessary and distracting. She is supposed to be precocious, but still--it seemed like she was a toddler with the vocabulary and sentence structure of a 20-year-old. But like I said, I didn’t care. I was a goner as soon as I read the first chapter.<br /><br />Okay, one final, teensy weensy, unimportant nit: What’s with the name Fikry?? It’s so hard to remember, let alone pronounce! My brain and mouth stumble. Is it Firkry or Frikry or Friky or what? Oh, okay, look up the title for the eighty gazillionth time. Oh, it’s FIKRY—I think. I sort of stutter when I recommend this title to someone, and I lose a little of my umph. And I need all my umph so I can sell it.<br /> <br />I get upset that people say this is a good beach read, or that it’s light and breezy. If a book moves along at a good pace, has an interesting plot, has somewhat happy characters, has no philosophical side roads, and is under 400 pages, is it classified as light? I don’t think that’s fair. This book has depth and wisdom. In my opinion, it’s top-notch literary fiction.<br /> <br />An added perk for me: I lived on Cape Cod for five years, and my husband worked on the ferry boats running to Hyannis. This book takes place on a fictional island near Hyannis and revolves around the fictional Island Books. I visited the islands many times and stopped in at bookstores that were a lot like Island Books, complete with wonderful owners who went out of their way to find the perfect book for me. Fond memories.<br /><br />I don’t allow myself to reread books, since I have too many new ones in my queue. But for this fantastic book, I might make an exception. Speaking of my book queue, I’d like to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13538873.Mr__Penumbra_s_24_Hour_Bookstore" title="Mr. Penumbra's 24-Hour Bookstore by Robin Sloan" rel="nofollow noopener">Mr. Penumbra's 24-Hour Bookstore</a> soon for comparison, though I know <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18293427.The_Storied_Life_of_A__J__Fikry" title="The Storied Life of A. J. Fikry by Gabrielle Zevin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Storied Life of A. J. Fikry</a> is going to be one hard act to follow.<br /><br />My friend’s daughter would be happy: I did go to paradise and I LOVED it. It was a fine, fine visit.<br /><br />HIGHLY recommended. 5 stars all the way, baby. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13026516594009435025" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_995934541" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/995934541" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3191832-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463550510p2/3191832.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/995934541?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/3191832-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3191832-lisa?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer995934541" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16816818807658510747">I remember being ten years old and all my friends really loving New Kids on the Block. I watched them all go crazy for it and I wanted in on this amazing, musical lifestyle. So I begged my mom to buy me the tape and she finally did. I listened to it on my purple boom box the whole way through, side A and side B. And when that tape ended I knew I was in a big pickle because.... I didn't like it.<br/><br/>You know where this is going.<br/><br/>So the next time we were all together, I worked up the nerve and confessed</span>
  <span id="freeText16816818807658510747" style="display:none">I remember being ten years old and all my friends really loving New Kids on the Block. I watched them all go crazy for it and I wanted in on this amazing, musical lifestyle. So I begged my mom to buy me the tape and she finally did. I listened to it on my purple boom box the whole way through, side A and side B. And when that tape ended I knew I was in a big pickle because.... I didn't like it.<br /><br />You know where this is going.<br /><br />So the next time we were all together, I worked up the nerve and confessed to my friends: I just don't like New Kids on the Block. I prepared for some major backlash, and... there was none. They were still my friends! (in fact, Lisa M.- the other Lisa - asked me if she could have my tape as a spare and I handed it right over, so I actually might have gained some points with her). <br /><br />The only difference in my New Kids story and my Fikry story is that I bought Fikry with my own money. I'm even going to pass along my copy to Kandice to enjoy and give out the stars freely and as she sees fit. I was happy that my friends were able to bond and get down to the musical stylings of The New Kids on the Block, and I'm just as delighted that all my Goodreads gals (oh, and guys! I have a few of them now, too!) loved this book. It wasn't for me. But I'm really, sincerely happy that it was for the majority of all of you.<br /><br />Now here are some more thoughts I have on this book, hidden by this spoiler tag for two reasons: #1. They contain (very light) spoilers. #2. They are my honest thoughts about this book, so I must preface this by saying: if you click on this spoiler, you are assuming the responsibility of not getting upset with me for not liking this book for these reasons. I completely respect any reader for loving this book. I just didn't, and these are my reasons:<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I really tried to like this book, but I did not like this book. I found the writing to be overly cutesy and I really don't dig that at all. In fact, truth be told, I thought the writing was pretty bad. Here's a great example of a part that I strongly disliked because of its cutesy-ness: <br /><br />"The second week of August, just before Maya starts kindergarten, she gets a matching set of glasses (round, red frames) and chicken pox (round, red bumps). A.J. curses the mother who had told him that the chicken pox vaccine was optional as the chicken pox is indeed a pox on their house".<br /><br />This is such a fantastic example of a style of writing that I really, really dislike. It has the feeling of trying entirely too hard. At this point I found it hard to go any further. I did though, but it was a push. <br /><br />I also found the whole book to be incredibly gimmicky. It felt to me like the sole purpose of writing this story was to have a vehicle that could carry all the book-lovers' jargon and literary references. I also disliked the tense the book was set in; I felt like by writing it in this way, it was reaching to be quirky and original. I really found the whole book to be a big reach to be quirky. It just didn't work at all for me. I'm pretty surprised that this book became a roaring hit. I know that a lot of my really good friends loved this book tremendously and recommended it to me, so I wanted to love it too. I always feel terribly bad when I dislike a book that profoundly touches another person that I care about. It just doesn't feel good. It makes me want to apologize! But I just can't pretend to like this book, even a little bit, because I felt like it was so poorly written and like I said already, gimmicky to the max. Also, it seems to be marked as a book that 'real' readers are going to rejoice over. To me that seems like a dirty sales trick: the literary equivalent of 'if you really loved me you'd do <i>whatever</i>'. Really, in my opinion, this is a rather poorly written book without much substance. I feel like the author is laughing all the way to the bank on this one. But my friends love it, and they are really smart and clever, much more so than me, so take all this with a grain of salt. But there you have it. Thanks in advance for not shunning me :)  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="16816818807658510747" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1185805509" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1185805509" />
    <a title="Nataliya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya"><img alt="Nataliya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605995014p2/3672777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1185805509?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nataliya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nataliya" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya">Nataliya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=2015-reads">2015-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1185805509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3133508237078769142">Unexpectedly and unabashedly charming. Cozy, sweet and life-affirming and yet somehow avoiding the overt sentimentality, managing to remain quietly refreshing and, again, charming in the nicest meaning of that word.<blockquote>
  <i>"The most annoying thing about it is that once a person gives a shit about one thing, he finds he has to start giving a shit about everything."</i>
</blockquote>It's a lovely quiet story about the way a life of a lonely and surly bookseller on a remote New England island gets turned around when he </span>
  <span id="freeText3133508237078769142" style="display:none">Unexpectedly and unabashedly charming. Cozy, sweet and life-affirming and yet somehow avoiding the overt sentimentality, managing to remain quietly refreshing and, again, charming in the nicest meaning of that word.<blockquote>
  <i>"The most annoying thing about it is that once a person gives a shit about one thing, he finds he has to start giving a shit about everything."</i>
</blockquote>It's a lovely quiet story about the way a life of a lonely and surly bookseller on a remote New England island gets turned around when he unexpectedly finds himself a guardian and then a father of an adorable toddler abandoned in his bookstore. It's a story of how one event can help reaffirm life and steer it into a completely new direction, soothing old wounds and opening new possibilities. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425015070i/13831108.jpg" width="390" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
<i>"What I say is, a town isn't a town without a bookstore. It may call itself a town, but unless it's got a bookstore it knows it's not fooling a soul."</i> ("American Gods" by Neil Gaiman)</blockquote>It's also a story of the world of book selling and book publishing, about the role a brick-and-mortar bookstore can - and should - play in a small community, about the love of books and the connections that they can help form. In the world of e-readers replacing 'dead tree' book and vanishing bookstores outcompeted by online retail giants this book is infused with optimism about the survival of the neighborhood bookstore - and what's more important, the simple necessity of such a survival. <br><br>Lovely and charming book that can generously give it's readers a few hours of quiet feel-good time - and who doesn't need these feelings from time to time? I know I do. <b>4 stars.</b><blockquote>
  <i>"We read to know we’re not alone. We read because we are alone. We read and we are not alone. We are not alone."</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="3133508237078769142" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1832069913" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1832069913" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1832069913?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1832069913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7491502829797848141">The Storied Life of A.J. Fikry by Gabrielle Zevin is a 2014 Algonquin Books publication. <br/><br/>Thanks to my Goodreads friend, Carol, for introducing me to this book! <br/><br/><br/> ISLAND BOOKS<br/> Alice Island’s Exclusive Provider of Fine Literary Content since 1999<br/><br/> “No Man Is an Island; Every Book Is a World”<br/><br/>This is the second ‘books about books’ novel I’ve read this week, and I have to say, it’s nice to know so many people share the same enthusiasm for books that I do. <br/><br/>This story is poignant and bittersweet, but is </span>
  <span id="freeText7491502829797848141" style="display:none">The Storied Life of A.J. Fikry by Gabrielle Zevin is a 2014 Algonquin Books publication. <br /><br />Thanks to my Goodreads friend, Carol, for introducing me to this book! <br /><br /><br /> ISLAND BOOKS<br /> Alice Island’s Exclusive Provider of Fine Literary Content since 1999<br /><br /> “No Man Is an Island; Every Book Is a World”<br /><br />This is the second ‘books about books’ novel I’ve read this week, and I have to say, it’s nice to know so many people share the same enthusiasm for books that I do. <br /><br />This story is poignant and bittersweet, but is also charming, touching and heartwarming. It’s a reader’s paradise and will soothe the brow of any book nerd who can’t help but feel a strong kinship with the characters, and maybe even recognize yourself in them just a little bit. <br /><br />A.J. owns and operates the independent books store, “Island Books”, located on Alice Island, Massachusetts, alone after his wife is killed in a car accident. As he stumbles through each day in a fog of bitter grief, a series of events snaps him to attention and his life takes on a new direction, one he never could have imagined. <br /><br />The first part of the book kept me in stitches. I’ve known literary snobs, and A.J. is one. I laughed out loud at his aversion to stocking Young Adult and children's books, and his opinion on series, and vampires. Then we got to the part where A.J. deals with customers and if you have worked in a bookstore or library you’ll relate, and again I’m laughing hysterically. <br /><br />“Why is any one book different from any other book? They are different, A.J. decides, because they are. We have to look inside many. We have to believe. We agree to be disappointed sometimes so that we can be exhilarated every now and again.”<br /><br />But, A.J.’s persnickety personality is soon softened by a very special surprise delivery to his shop, which gives him a new perspective on life and relationships, including one with the book sales representative, Amelia, who warms up to A.J. after getting off to a pretty rough start, and the local chief of police who becomes one of his best friends. <br /><br />The story is like an homage to book lovers, reading, and the way books shape us and the impact they can have on our outlook on life, even in our relationships, our attitudes, and how they can inspire us through good and bad times. <br /><br />I loved A.J. right from the start. I understood where he was in life at that very moment, and while I snickered at his drollness, his deadpan introverted nature, my heart broke for him.<br /> <br />It was an honor to watch him come back to life and embrace it with as much gusto has he could muster. Seeing his life enriched in such an amazing way was only part of the story. A.J. and his little bookstore also touched and enriched other’s lives all of them had a life much better than the one they would have had without him. He built an important legacy over the years, and that legacy, thanks to those he loved, will go on to extend the love of books and reading to people for a long time to come… even to those who love vampires, series, Young Adult, and Children’s books about orphans.<br /><br />This a delightful story that lifted my spirits and warmed my heart. <br /><br />5 stars<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7491502829797848141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_944581870" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/944581870" />
    <a title="Idarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1283951-idarah"><img alt="Idarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596863879p2/1283951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/944581870?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Idarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Idarah" href="/user/show/1283951-idarah">Idarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1283951-idarah?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1283951-idarah?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer944581870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13915037479069771360"><blockquote>
  <b>"A question I’ve thought about a great deal is why it is so much easier to write about the things we dislike/hate/ acknowledge to be flawed than the things we love." – A.J. Fikry</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I stayed up late last night to finish this book, and hoped that by the time I woke up this morning, I'd have a clear idea about why and what I loved most about this book. I'm still at a loss for words because I love every single part of this book! <br/><br/>Fittingly, it was recommended by the owner of a tiny independent books</span>
  <span id="freeText13915037479069771360" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>"A question I’ve thought about a great deal is why it is so much easier to write about the things we dislike/hate/ acknowledge to be flawed than the things we love." – A.J. Fikry</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />I stayed up late last night to finish this book, and hoped that by the time I woke up this morning, I'd have a clear idea about why and what I loved most about this book. I'm still at a loss for words because I love every single part of this book! <br /><br />Fittingly, it was recommended by the owner of a tiny independent bookstore in my neighborhood, one of the few of its kind left in Dallas. I didn't read the synopsis, and I tried to avoid reviews that mentioned particulars about plot. I wanted to be thoroughly surpised and amazed, just like readers of long ago, who'd ask for a copy of their favorite author's next book to be set aside at their local bookstore as soon as it arrived–days before dustjackets, ereaders, and internet pop-up ads. Blind faith can move you to take <i>good</i> risks.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>"Why is any one book different from any other book? They are different, A.J. decides, because they are. We have to look inside many. We have to believe. We agree to be disappointed sometimes so that we can be exhilarated every now and again."</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Well, that's it really. I loved this book because it was exhilarating. It was a book about books and people who love them–people of all shapes, colors and sizes. It also encompassed my ideas of hope, love, family, grief, and <i>reality</i>, really. A book that makes you laugh heartily, sniffle into your coffee, and reread the acknowledgement page, must be a book of upstanding character. I applaude you, Gabrielle Zevin. Thank you for rocking my world! Let's meet up for drinks, my treat!<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13915037479069771360" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1273065065" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1273065065" />
    <a title="Dolors" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18383778-dolors"><img alt="Dolors" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502350013p2/18383778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1273065065?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dolors" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dolors" href="/user/show/18383778-dolors">Dolors</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/21445677-the-storied-life-of-a-j-fikry">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Book lovers of all ages and literary tastes</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Dolors by: </span>
      Zevin
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18383778-dolors?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1273065065" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer581752437778408633">I don’t know how many times my eyes skimmed through this title in the last years, reminding me vaguely of how much I loved <i>Margarettown</i> in what seems like a lifetime ago, and how easily I discarded it, thinking I wouldn’t find it worthy after the more literary works I’ve come to read since I joined GR.<br/>How arrogant of me.<br/><br/>This is a simple book to read. A page turner with short chapters, written in a fast, light-hearted prose that sounds so natural and easy-going that you’ll forget you are reading </span>
  <span id="freeText581752437778408633" style="display:none">I don’t know how many times my eyes skimmed through this title in the last years, reminding me vaguely of how much I loved <i>Margarettown</i> in what seems like a lifetime ago, and how easily I discarded it, thinking I wouldn’t find it worthy after the more literary works I’ve come to read since I joined GR.<br />How arrogant of me.<br /><br />This is a simple book to read. A page turner with short chapters, written in a fast, light-hearted prose that sounds so natural and easy-going that you’ll forget you are reading a book. Instead, you’ll feel like you are sharing cozy conversation with an old friend who is a book nerd like you.<br />And yes, you guessed it just right. <br />The novel is full of cliches. <br />A quaint bookstore located in a small island near the cost of Maine.<br />Plenty of quoted authors and works that will bring you delightful memories and spontaneous smiles.<br />A curmudgeon bookseller who lost his wife in a car accident.<br />A publishing sales rep with good reading tastes and a disastrous love life.<br />A cad disguised as a writer with a single book to prove for his talent.<br />A baby girl who offers a second chance to the young widower and brings life back to the island’s bookstore and its inhabitants.<br />But who cares about cliches when a story tugs at one’s heartstrings and sings a full symphony, with pauses and silences between powerful movements? <br />Particularly if love and only love is the dominant tune of this moving story.<br />Love of words, love of books, love of literature, love of people, love of improbable dreams… And ultimately, love of life.<br /><br />I will save you the rave I could come up with quite promptly as I just turned the last page of this heart-warming novel and my heart is overbrimming with ache and tenderness for its characters. I wasn’t expecting such an intense ending but it culminated what had been an increasingly gratifying read.<br />I will just say that I connected to this endearing story in multiple levels and that any person who loves literature will be touched by Zevin’s passion for books and by her frank eagerness to connect with those at the other side of the page. <br />What a rare gift, to be reminded of the reasons why I fell in love with books in the first place and of the importance of spreading this love like gospel. <br />Ride on, Zevin, ride on.<br /><br /><i>“We aren’t the things we collect, acquire, read. We are, for as long as we are here, only love. The things we loved. The people we loved. And these, I think these really do live on.” </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="581752437778408633" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2o9GfgACeIhJXycardwZVHN9KYGQDQlF1LF03AWpZ/RSRojrPn6HNsWzyI/w7waSlFm28AXbRPw5irvBqYcynQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jmXfC9Jrt2z3hqBLybqNCc1PaCnbUxmLJNoiEQrcS2AGrBGe7BdI0ntqT96UiZLPKmv3WE6FVDLJ4e0MpvIeCQ==')})
  }

She befriends hardscrabble and complex fellow Kentuckians, and is fiercely determined to bring comfort and joy, instill literacy, and give to those who have nothing, a bookly respite, a fleeting retreat to faraway lands.\n\nInspired by the true and historical blue-skinned people of Kentucky and the brave and dedicated Kentucky Pack Horse library service, The Book Woman of Troublesome Creek       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/40593.Gabrielle_Zevin">About Gabrielle Zevin</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/40593.Gabrielle_Zevin"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1503541462p3/40593.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/40593.Gabrielle_Zevin">Gabrielle Zevin
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
4,580
followers
</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2031963993827918255">GABRIELLE ZEVIN is an internationally bestselling author whose books have sold millions of copies and been translated into over thirty languages.<br/><br/>Her eighth novel, The Storied Life of A.J. Fikry (2014), spent months on the New York Times Bestseller List, reached #1 on the National Indie Best Seller List, and has been a bestseller all around the world. The Toronto Globe and Mail called the book “a p</span>
  <span id="freeText2031963993827918255" style="display:none">GABRIELLE ZEVIN is an internationally bestselling author whose books have sold millions of copies and been translated into over thirty languages.<br /><br />Her eighth novel, The Storied Life of A.J. Fikry (2014), spent months on the New York Times Bestseller List, reached #1 on the National Indie Best Seller List, and has been a bestseller all around the world. The Toronto Globe and Mail called the book “a powerful novel about the power of novels.” Her debut, Margarettown, was a selection of the Barnes &amp; Noble Discover Great New Writers program. The Hole We’re In was a New York Times Editor’s Choice title.<br /><br />She has also written books for young readers. Her best known young adult novel is Elsewhere, an American Library Association Notable Children’s Book. Of Elsewhere, the New York Times Book Review wrote, “Every so often a book comes along with a premise so fresh and arresting it seems to exist in a category all its own… Elsewhere, by Gabrielle Zevin, is such a book.”<br /><br />She is the screenwriter of Conversations with Other Women (Helena Bonham Carter, Aaron Eckhart) for which she received an Independent Spirit Award Nomination for Best First Screenplay. In 2009, she and director Hans Canosa adapted her novel Memoirs of a Teenage Amnesiac (ALA Best Books for Young Adults) into the Japanese film, Dareka ga Watashi ni Kiss wo Shita. She has occasionally written criticism for the New York Times Book Review and NPR’s All Things Considered, and she began her writing career at age fourteen as a music critic for the Fort Lauderdale Sun-Sentinel.<br />Zevin is a graduate of Harvard University. She lives in Los Angeles. Her ninth novel is Young Jane Young.<br /><br />NOTE: Apologies, but I don't reply to messages on Goodreads.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2031963993827918255" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
